</header><div class="entry-content"><div class="tasty-pins-hidden-image-container" style="display:none;"><img alt="Bowls of our Korean Bibimbap recipe made with a fried egg" class="tasty-pins-hidden-image" data-pin-description="How to Make Korean Bibimbap with brown rice, veggies, and a fried egg! <p>Any time I eat bibimbap it takes me back to the first time we visited South Korea in 2013. It was our first trip abroad and we visited friends who showed us around and taught us the way of bibimbap, which means “mixed rice” in Korean.</p>
<p>Let me show you my inspired take with this Easy Bibimbap with Gochujang Sauce—perfect for weeknight meals, hosting, and beyond!</p>
<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter"><img alt="Wood cutting board with brown rice, vegetables, and an egg ready to show How to Make Korean Bibimbap" class="wp-image-43462" data-jpibfi-post-excerpt="" data-jpibfi-post-title="Easy Bibimbap with Gochujang Sauce" data-jpibfi-post-url="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-bibimbap-with-gochujang-sauce/" data-jpibfi-src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/How-to-Make-Korean-Bibimbap-with-brown-rice-veggies-and-a-fried-egg-Plus-a-quick-recipe-for-Gochujang-sauce-bibimbap-korean-glutenfree-minimalistbaker-recipe-NEW.jpg" data-pin-description="How to Make Korean Bibimbap with brown rice, veggies, and a fried egg! <span id="more-43427"></span>
<h3>What is Bibimbap?</h3>
<p>Bibimbap is a traditional Korean dish comprised of rice, a mixture of vegetables, an egg, and sometimes meat, often served in a hot stone bowl. It’s typically served with sauce, my favorite being Gochujang.</p>
<h3>What is Gochujang?</h3>
<p>Gochujang is a spicy-sweet Korean sauce that’s typically made of a blend of chilies, glutinous rice, salt, and fermented soybeans. <strong>Because most brands are not gluten-free I made my own <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-gochujang-sauce-korean-chili-paste/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">vegan Gochujang recipe</a></strong> and have to say it’s quite close to the real thing! Plus, it only requires <strong>1 blender, 5 ingredients, and 5 minutes to prepare</strong>.</p>
<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter"><img alt="Platter of perfectly cooked vegetables for making Korean Bibimbap" class="wp-image-43439" data-jpibfi-post-excerpt="" data-jpibfi-post-title="Easy Bibimbap with Gochujang Sauce" data-jpibfi-post-url="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-bibimbap-with-gochujang-sauce/" data-jpibfi-src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/How-to-Make-Korean-Bibimbap-with-brown-rice-veggies-and-a-fried-egg-Plus-a-quick-recipe-for-Gochujang-sauce-bibimbap-korean-glutenfree-minimalistbaker-recipe-5.jpg" data-pin-description="How to Make Korean Bibimbap with brown rice, veggies, and a fried egg! Plus, a quick recipe for Gochujang sauce! #bibimbap #korean #glutenfree #minimalistbaker #recipe" data-pin-title="Easy Bibimbap with Gochujang Sauce" sizes="(max-width: 960px) 100vw, (max-width: 1149px) 590px, 720px" src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/How-to-Make-Korean-Bibimbap-with-brown-rice-veggies-and-a-fried-egg-Plus-a-quick-recipe-for-Gochujang-sauce-bibimbap-korean-glutenfree-minimalistbaker-recipe-5.jpg" srcset="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/How-to-Make-Korean-Bibimbap-with-brown-rice-veggies-and-a-fried-egg-Plus-a-quick-recipe-for-Gochujang-sauce-bibimbap-korean-glutenfree-minimalistbaker-recipe-5.jpg 1456w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/How-to-Make-Korean-Bibimbap-with-brown-rice-veggies-and-a-fried-egg-Plus-a-quick-recipe-for-Gochujang-sauce-bibimbap-korean-glutenfree-minimalistbaker-recipe-5-200x300.jpg 200w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/How-to-Make-Korean-Bibimbap-with-brown-rice-veggies-and-a-fried-egg-Plus-a-quick-recipe-for-Gochujang-sauce-bibimbap-korean-glutenfree-minimalistbaker-recipe-5-768x1152.jpg 768w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/How-to-Make-Korean-Bibimbap-with-brown-rice-veggies-and-a-fried-egg-Plus-a-quick-recipe-for-Gochujang-sauce-bibimbap-korean-glutenfree-minimalistbaker-recipe-5-683x1024.jpg 683w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/How-to-Make-Korean-Bibimbap-with-brown-rice-veggies-and-a-fried-egg-Plus-a-quick-recipe-for-Gochujang-sauce-bibimbap-korean-glutenfree-minimalistbaker-recipe-5-600x900.jpg 600w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/How-to-Make-Korean-Bibimbap-with-brown-rice-veggies-and-a-fried-egg-Plus-a-quick-recipe-for-Gochujang-sauce-bibimbap-korean-glutenfree-minimalistbaker-recipe-5-680x1020.jpg 680w"/></figure></div>
<p>My take on bibimbap requires just <strong>10 ingredients to make</strong> and comes together quite quickly, especially if you’ve already <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/how-to-cook-brown-rice-2-ways/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">cooked your brown rice</a> and made (or purchased) your <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-gochujang-sauce-korean-chili-paste/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Gochujang sauce</a>.</p>
<h3>What vegetables are in Bibimbap?</h3>
<p>Aside from cooked rice, bibimbap typically comes with a variety of cooked vegetables with various preparations. But to keep things simple for a weeknight meal, I simply sautéed bean sprouts, green onion, carrots, zucchini, and fresh spinach in a little sesame oil and coconut aminos (or sub tamari or sea salt), and topped with a sprinkle of sesame seeds.</p>
<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter"><img alt="Saucepan of freshly cooked fluffy brown rice for homemade Korean Bibimbap" class="wp-image-43437" data-jpibfi-post-excerpt="" data-jpibfi-post-title="Easy Bibimbap with Gochujang Sauce" data-jpibfi-post-url="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-bibimbap-with-gochujang-sauce/" data-jpibfi-src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/How-to-Make-Korean-Bibimbap-with-brown-rice-veggies-and-a-fried-egg-Plus-a-quick-recipe-for-Gochujang-sauce-bibimbap-korean-glutenfree-minimalistbaker-recipe-3.jpg" data-pin-description="How to Make Korean Bibimbap with brown rice, veggies, and a fried egg! <figure><iframe allowfullscreen="allowfullscreen" frameborder="0" height="380" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/fTysq5mUuw4" width="680"></iframe></figure>
<h3>Do you need a dolsot (hot stone bowl) for serving Bibimbap?</h3>
<p>Traditionally, bibimbap is served in a hot stone bowl called a <a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B00KFMTLQ2/?creativeASIN=B000TYBWIG&amp;linkCode=w61&amp;imprToken=8TKuZKuAeXDUkyJDRZohAQ&amp;slotNum=4&amp;tag=minimalistbaker-20" rel="noopener nofollow noreferrer" target="_blank">dolsot</a>, which allows you to assemble the bibimbap and then heat the underside so the rice gets browned and crispy. Yum.</p>
<p>However, you can either skip the dolsot and use a basic serving bowl o<em>r</em> my little hack is to stir fry your cooked rice in a little sesame oil until crispy and brown before serving so it gets some added crunch and texture.</p>
<h3>Is Bibimbap vegetarian?</h3>
<p>Depending on the ingredients in the Gochujang sauce and whether or not it’s served with meat, bibimbap <em>can</em> be vegetarian when served with an egg. We opted for a perfect fried egg, but also suggest some vegan options below that are just as delicious.</p>

<p>We hope you LOVE this inspired take on bibimbap! It’s:</p>
<p>Quick &amp; easy to make<strong><br/></strong>Colorful<br/>Customizable<br/>Comforting<br/>&amp; Delicious</p>
<p>This would make the perfect weeknight meal or for hosting, as it’s customizable with protein and vegetable topping options. The Gochujang sauce isn’t overly spicy either, so it’s even great for guests with more sensitive palates.</p>
<p>Need ideas for what to serve this with? How about some <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-kimchi/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Homemade Vegan Kimchi</a>, <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/gochujang-stir-fried-brussels-sprouts/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Gochujang Stir-Fried Brussels Sprouts</a>, or <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/spicy-korean-style-cauliflower-wings/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Gochujang-Spiced Cauliflower Wings</a>?!</p>
<p class="p1">If you try this recipe, let us know! Leave a comment, rate it, and don’t forget to tag a photo <a href="https://www.instagram.com/minimalistbaker/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">#minimalistbaker</a> on Instagram. Cheers, friends!</p>

<h2 class="wprm-recipe-name">Easy Bibimbap with Gochujang Sauce</h2>
<div class="wprm-recipe-summary">
<p>A Korean-inspired dish that’s simple, healthy, and customizable depending on the season. It’s also an affordable meal and the sauce can be made ahead of time to ensure speedy future preparations! Add some homemade (or store-bought) kimchi for the ultimate feast. Just 10 ingredients required.</p> </div>

<div class="wprm-recipe-ingredients-container">
<h3 class="wprm-recipe-header">Ingredients</h3>
<div class="wprm-unit-conversion-container"><a class="wprm-unit-conversion wprmpuc-active" data-recipe="43428" data-system="1" href="#">US Customary</a> – <a class="wprm-unit-conversion" data-recipe="43428" data-system="2" href="#">Metric</a></div> <div class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-group">
<h4 class="wprm-recipe-group-name wprm-recipe-ingredient-group-name">RICE</h4>
<ul class="wprm-recipe-ingredients">
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">3/4</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">cup</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">short-grain brown or white rice, rinsed</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(soaking for 12-24 hours to speed cooking is optional*)</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">1 ½</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">cups</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">water </span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(if rice was soaked, reduce water by about 1/4 cup (60 ml) as recipe is written)</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">1</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">pinch</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">sea salt</span>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-group">
<h4 class="wprm-recipe-group-name wprm-recipe-ingredient-group-name">VEGGIES + EGG</h4>
<ul class="wprm-recipe-ingredients">
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">2-3</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">Tbsp</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">sesame oil, <strong>DIVIDED</strong></span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(toasted for more flavor, untoasted works, too*)</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">3</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">cups</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">packed mixed vegetables </span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(such as finely shredded carrot, thinly sliced zucchini, or spinach)</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">1</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">heaping cup</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">bean sprouts </span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(if you can’t find, sub more mixed vegetables)</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">2</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">stalks</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">green onion, sliced on an angle</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">2</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">cloves</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">garlic, minced</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">2</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">Tbsp</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name"><a href="https://aax-us-east.amazon-adsystem.com/x/c/QmX1rdK-bLlyB7OiaLX9FdoAAAFq1h7YdAEAAAFKAfDf3o8/https://www.amazon.com/Coconut-Secret-Raw-Aminos-Pack/dp/B00CMYMRL2/?creativeASIN=B00CMYMRL2&amp;linkCode=w61&amp;imprToken=JDynMtbiS3V1q2UJrcHLUg&amp;slotNum=38&amp;tag=minimalistbaker-20" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">coconut aminos, <strong>DIVIDED</strong></a></span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(or sub tamari to taste, or sea salt)</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">2</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">large</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">eggs* </span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(we recommend organic, pasture-raised, and as ethically sourced as possible, such as Vital Farms)</span>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-group">
<h4 class="wprm-recipe-group-name wprm-recipe-ingredient-group-name">FOR SERVING</h4>
<ul class="wprm-recipe-ingredients">
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">2-4</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">Tbsp</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name"><a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-gochujang-sauce-korean-chili-paste/" target="_blank">Korean Gochujang Sauce </a></span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(or sub store-bought — look for vegan or gluten-free as needed, such as <a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B00O2RXEVY/?creativeASIN=B000TYBWIG&amp;linkCode=w61&amp;imprToken=s6rvQ5gcWhZ87VhxCkc2ww&amp;slotNum=4&amp;tag=minimalistbaker-20" target="_blank">Wholly Gochujang</a>)</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name"><a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-kimchi/" target="_blank">Kimchi</a></span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(<strong><em>optional</em></strong>)</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">Toasted or raw sesame seeds</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(<strong><em>optional</em></strong>)</span>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
<div class="wprm-recipe-instructions-container">
<h3 class="wprm-recipe-header">Instructions</h3>
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-group">
<ol class="wprm-recipe-instructions">
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text"><p>Optional: If soaking rice, rinse, drain, and add to a mixing bowl and cover with cool water. Soak for 12 hours or overnight. For a quicker soak, cover in hot water for 1 hour. Then rinse and drain.</p></div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text"><p>To a medium saucepan, add cooking water (if you soaked your rice, start with 1 ¼  cups water as recipe is written), rinsed rice, and salt. Heat over high heat and bring to a boil, reduce heat to simmer, and cover. Cook for 15-20 minutes or until water is absorbed and rice is tender and fluffy. Soaked rice generally takes less time to cook. Unsoaked rice can take up to 30 minutes or more. Keep covered and set aside.</p></div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">In the meantime, prepare <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-gochujang-sauce-korean-chili-paste/" target="_blank">Gochujang sauce</a>. Skip if using store-bought.</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">While the rice finishes cooking, heat a large skillet over medium heat (stainless steel or cast iron are best). Once hot, add 1 tsp of sesame oil or enough to just coat the pan.</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text"><p>Once the oil is hot, add vegetables one type at a time and cook in batches until lightly browned (1-2 minutes), seasoning each with a little minced garlic and a dash of coconut aminos, tamari, or sea salt. Cooking in batches allows you to arrange vegetables separately over the rice for visual effect. We cooked the zucchini first, then carrots, green onion, bean sprouts, and spinach. Add more oil to the pan as needed between vegetables.</p></div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text"><p>Arrange cooked vegetables in individual piles on a serving plate and cover gently to keep warm until serving.</p></div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text"><p>To cook eggs (if vegan, see notes for options!), heat the same pan over medium heat. Once hot, add a little more oil (sesame or otherwise), and carefully crack eggs. For sunny-side up (our preference), cover briefly with a lid to steam for 1 minute, then remove lid and continue cooking until whites are cooked but yolks are still runny. Turn off heat and set aside (uncovered).</p></div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">To serve, divide desired amount of rice between serving bowls (see notes for traditional <a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B00KFMTLQ2/?creativeASIN=B000TYBWIG&amp;linkCode=w61&amp;imprToken=8TKuZKuAeXDUkyJDRZohAQ&amp;slotNum=4&amp;tag=minimalistbaker-20" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">dolsot recommendations</a> and crispy rice hacks!) and top with portions of cooked veggies and egg.</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">Serve with 1-2 Tbsp Gochujang, kimchi (optional), and a dash of sesame seeds (optional). Bibimbap means “mixed rice,” so once your egg and Gochujang sauce are added, use a spoon or your chopsticks to stir everything together and mix the flavors. Then enjoy!</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text"><p>This dish is best fresh, but leftovers can be stored in the refrigerator up to 2 days and be reheated on the stovetop over medium heat as a stir fry. Not freezer-friendly.</p></div>
</li>
</ol>
</div>
</div>
<div class="wprm-recipe-video-container">
<h3 class="wprm-recipe-header"></h3>
<iframe allow="accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="380" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/fTysq5mUuw4" width="680"></iframe> </div>
<div class="wprm-recipe-notes-container">
<h3 class="wprm-recipe-header">Notes</h3>
<p>*Soaking rice not included in prep time.<br>*Sesame oil can be found at Asian markets and most grocery stores and is fairly affordable. Its flavor really works best in this recipe and either toasted or untoasted can be used. But it can be subbed with avocado or refined coconut oil for a similar result (don’t use virgin coconut oil or the dish will taste like coconut).<br>*<strong>If vegan</strong>, omit the egg and sub our <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/baked-crispy-peanut-tofu/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Crispy Baked Peanut Tofu</a>, Quick Scrambled Tofu (similar to the tofu in <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/noodle-free-pad-thai-30-minutes/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">this recipe</a>), or just double up on veggies!<br>*<strong>To keep this bowl grain-free</strong>, omit grains and double up on veggies or sub <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/how-to-make-cauliflower-rice/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">cauliflower rice</a>!<br>*In this recipe we served the bibimbap in bowls, but you can purchase <a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B00KFMTLQ2/?creativeASIN=B000TYBWIG&amp;linkCode=w61&amp;imprToken=8TKuZKuAeXDUkyJDRZohAQ&amp;slotNum=4&amp;tag=minimalistbaker-20" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank">Korean-style dolsot</a> bowls, which allow you to cook the bibimbap after plating to get the rice crispy on the bottom of the bowl. However, for a similar effect, simply stir fry rice in a little sesame oil in a hot pan for a few minutes, tossing occasionally, until toasty and golden brown.<br/>*Nutrition information is a rough estimate calculated with equal amounts of carrot, zucchini, and spinach for the mixed vegetables, with lesser amounts of sesame oil and Gochujang sauce, and without optional ingredients.<br/>*Recipe method adapted from the amazing <a href="https://www.maangchi.com/recipe/bibimbap" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank">Maangchi</a>, and inspired by our many bowls of bibimbap while <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/dining-guide-shanghai-seoul-japan/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">visiting South Korea</a>!</br></br></br></br></p>
</div>
<div class="wprm-recipe-nutrition-container">
<h3 class="wprm-recipe-header">Nutrition Per Serving (1 of 2 Servings) </h3><ul><li><strong>Calories:</strong> 519 <li><strong>Fat:</strong> 22g <li><strong>Saturated fat:</strong> 3.8g <li><strong>Sodium:</strong> 528mg <li><strong>Potassium:</strong> 668mg <li><strong>Carbohydrates:</strong> 73.2g <li><strong>Fiber:</strong> 8.9g <li><strong>Sugar:</strong> 12.5g <li><strong>Protein:</strong> 14.9g</li></li></li></li></li></li></li></li></li></ul> </div>

<article id="article-comment-829789">

<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Becca" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/6562d0baf62bdf1d92a331d6701054a9?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/6562d0baf62bdf1d92a331d6701054a9?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Becca" width="96"><span itemprop="name">Becca</span> <span class="says">says</span> </img></p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-bibimbap-with-gochujang-sauce/?t=1582394659#comment-829789">September 22, 2019 at 6:28 pm</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>This was so tasty! I used all the veggies suggested in the recipe, but I subbed tamari for coconut aminos as it’s what I had on hand. I ended up opting for a store bought gochujang sauce to save time, and it was good still! A lot spicier than I expected actually, I think i’d stick to maybe 1/2-1tbsp instead of 1-2.</p>
<p>I’m reheating some for my lunch tomorrow (and we only have a microwave at work) so fingers crossed it stays somewhat delicious without the fresh out of the fry-pan texture.</p>

<p>I was so nervous to make this because of how much Korean chili goes in the sauce! I wasn’t able to find Korean chili anywhere so I ended up using mostly chili powder and some cayenne and closer to 1/4 cup because I was nervous. This recipe is so tasty!! Thank you minimalist baker for inspiring me to leave my comfort zone, I don’t think I’ve ever eaten something labeled as “Korean food” and I’m so glad I made this. Yum!</p>

<li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 wpr_havequestion_li" id="comment-805682">
<article id="article-comment-805682">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for NPF" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/37ef3052bdcda39378c59e2f2fb79095?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/37ef3052bdcda39378c59e2f2fb79095?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for NPF" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">NPF</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-bibimbap-with-gochujang-sauce/?t=1582394659#comment-805682">May 26, 2019 at 1:47 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>Hi Dana,<br/>
I am a follow of your recipes, and admittedly was upset about the transition of this site to contain animal products. Your website and cookbook have been very helpful in my own journey as a home cook. I know this doesn’t have to do with this recipe specifically, but as someone who has been operating in and advocating for “plant based” eating for so long, why have you decided to change course? I understand that you don’t want to reveal some personal health issues, but considering your impact on the food community, a more detailed explanation would be helpful. Also can you explain what “ethically Sourced” means with regards to supporting the egg industry?<br/>
Thanks</p>
</div>
<div class="comment-reply"><a aria-label="Reply to NPF" class="comment-reply-link" data-belowelement="comment-805682" data-commentid="805682" data-postid="43427" data-respondelement="respond" href="#comment-805682" rel="nofollow">Reply</a></div>
</article>
<ul class="children">
<li class="comment byuser comment-author-dana bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-805734">
<article id="article-comment-805734">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Dana @ Minimalist Baker" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/c7caa94d71e10eb485999d00c6e9b624?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/c7caa94d71e10eb485999d00c6e9b624?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Dana @ Minimalist Baker" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Dana @ Minimalist Baker</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-bibimbap-with-gochujang-sauce/?t=1582394659#comment-805734">May 26, 2019 at 9:36 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>Hi there, thanks for the question. I want to clarify a few things: Minimalist Baker started first and foremost as a simple food blog, with recipes that included meat, eggs, dairy, and gluten. Then, early on I removed dairy from my diet for digestive relief, so the recipes became dairy-free. Then, I started adding gluten-free recipes as some of my friends were sensitive to gluten, and I later became sensitive myself. Then, later I became interested in plant-based recipes, primarily for health reasons, and so the recipes took a turn in that direction. </p>
<p>I never shared that I was a vegan, although I did eat primarily vegan off and on for a few years and enjoyed experimenting with recipes in this realm. However, ultimately, I felt my body was asking for more nourishment and at the recommendation of several physicians, I recently decided to add animal products back into my diet. </p>
<p>The recipes have never been strictly one specific diet or another, but have rather been a loose reflection of what I’m interested in / going through diet- and health-wise at the moment, which is naturally always in flux. I have to trust that the creativity that comes from what I’m interested in or going through at the moment will in some way help or inspire our audience in some way. And I also acknowledge that this audience may grow and change and be in flux itself over the years, just as I am. I know for some it was surprising to see we’d be adding eggs and meat back in, but as we see it, it’s just another season of sharing what food excites and nourishes me right now. </p>
<p>I don’t care to go into any more of my personal health history on the internet. I hope you understanding that in doing so, it opens me up to a lot of scrutiny, opinions, and medical advice that aren’t helpful because no one really knows my health situation besides me and my doctors. </p>
<p>As for ethically-sourced eggs, I understand that some vegans believe there is no such thing as an ethically-sourced egg, so let’s just start with acknowledging that. But for me personally, I think ethically-sourced eggs are organic, pasture-raised, non-GMO, and free-range, which is about the best you can do unless you get eggs from your own chickens or a neighbor’s chickens. I buy eggs primarily from Vital Farms.</p>
<p>I hope that sheds some light and clarity on this transition.</p>
</div>

<div class="comment-content">
<p>One of my favorite recipes in months. My husband was getting a little sick of MB’s enchiladas (which are also all amazing). I left off the egg on mine, no tofu substitution necessary!<br/>
Not to add too much to comments not related to this recipe, but I am excited about this transition. I’ve been eating vegetarian and more recently vegan for most of my life, and it’s often been difficult to find recipes traditional meat eaters will enjoy. Having so many wonderful plant-based recipes intermixed with some recipes that include egg and meat makes the blog as a whole more accessible to people who may otherwise be afraid to try out a “vegan blog.” Thank you for continuing to (freely) share such inspired creations! I will continue to buy the cookbooks and recommend you to all eaters looking for a great food blog.</p>

<div class="comment-content">
<p>Dana, thanks for all the lovely recipes!<br/>
Wanted to also give support and say thanks for making it so easy to make any of your recipes vegan or vegetarian. You are clearly still supporting others having a fully plant based diet!<br/>
If we are honest, the reason the meat industry has turned to mass producing and related unethical practices is due to so many Americans (and certain other countries) demanding way more meat than is needed or healthy. Adding a moderate amount of meat to an also veggie filled diet is a sustainable practice. I am hoping those meat-eaters who are looking for healthier ways to cook will find your site. We each have to find what’s best for ourselves and I commend you for listening to your body. May peace be with you.</p>

<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 wpr_madethis_li" id="comment-805050">
<article id="article-comment-805050">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Maria" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/83517ae9c457d450b32f87ff6fc3a233?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/83517ae9c457d450b32f87ff6fc3a233?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Maria" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Maria</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-bibimbap-with-gochujang-sauce/?t=1582394659#comment-805050">May 22, 2019 at 3:53 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>This is excellent–your version of gochujang is such a revelation. I started making the sauce when you first posted it; I love gochujang and to find a recipe that is not only simple but this wildly delicious and digestible, was a real gift. It’s great, too, with roasted vegetables. I’ve never commented on this blog before, but I’ve been visiting here for years and have used countless of your wonderful recipes. FOR FREE, I might add. I’ve printed out so many of them that I suspect they amount to a full cookbook. Thank you–utterly. Your inventiveness, and delight in food and people, shines through. I’m sorry that you’ve been treated poorly simply because of your decision to align your blog with your life. Many of the commenters who have turned away have missed an opportunity to exercise the compassion that is at the heart of being vegan (and eating in general, I would think), and the chance to learn flexibility. They’ve forgotten, too, that they have enjoyed your recipes while you have asked nothing of them. Thank you, Dana. I’ll be back, many, many times and look forward to your recipes.</p>

<p>Oh dear, I didn’t realize that the recipes weren’t vegan any more and have been recommending the website to friends. I must have missed a post or something. It’s disappointing for sure, as animal-based recipe websites are a dime a dozen, and it’s nice to not have to wade through those sites looking for “special” recipes or “here’s a picture of bacon, but vegans can substitute tofu!” BUT I have appreciated the recipes over the years, and even though I’m not going to be following you or buying your cookbooks any more, I sincerely hope that this pays off for you in the end (money-wise and health-wise).</p>

<p>We recently announced we plan to incorporate recipes that aren’t vegan, including meat and eggs. However, you can update your email subscription to receive only vegan recipes (do so at the bottom of any email we’ve sent you). And you can always access our vegan recipes <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/recipe-index/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">here</a> by selecting “vegan” under “special diet.” We understand if we’re no longer a good fit for you. Thanks for your support thus far!</p>

<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 wpr_havequestion_li" id="comment-804928">
<article id="article-comment-804928">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Hana" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d47dd4c2bb48eef04d1b2d31ab6db7f5?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d47dd4c2bb48eef04d1b2d31ab6db7f5?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Hana" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Hana</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-bibimbap-with-gochujang-sauce/?t=1582394659#comment-804928">May 21, 2019 at 11:43 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>I feel sad.</p>
<p>Firstly, I’m sad that a plant-based diet wasn’t able to support you in your health and that you’ve had to make the difficult decision to reincorporate animal products back into your diet. I wish you all the best and hope that this change is able to provide the healing that you are looking for.</p>
<p>Secondly, I feel sad about the message this portrays to the world; that a plant-based diet is insufficient to maintain good health and that someone with such influence as yourself is choosing to promote animal products despite the harm to the environment, animals, and overall health.</p>
<p>Thirdly, I feel sad because you are the reason that I made the change towards a plant-based diet. I found your blog a couple of years ago and have introduced all of my family and many friends to it, many of whom have also made the switch to plant-based eating. I love your recipes, your photography and your overall message of promoting health and well-being through food. I’m sad that I no longer feel the same joy that I used to because it no longer feels personal to me. I feel like I’ve lost a role model and a friend. I realise it sounds dramatic, but it was not an easy change for me to make, and you were instrumental in it. Now this just feels like any other food blog.</p>
<p>Finally, I’m sad about a lot of the negative and even cruel responses you’ve received. I know that the plant-based and vegan communities are very passionate about what we believe, but that’s never an excuse to treat people poorly. I hope you can understand that most vegans are compassionate people and don’t support cruelty, emotional or otherwise.</p>
</div>

<div class="comment-content">
<p>Hi Becky, sorry for any confusion. This year we have decided to begin broadening the scope of our recipes beyond strictly plant-based not only to accommodate more people’s dietary needs, but also in order to be more transparent about the way my diet has shifted in the last year to better support my health. </p>
<p>We will continue to share plenty of plant-based recipes (which can always be found <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/recipe-index/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">here</a> by selecting the “vegan” option under “Special Diet”). But we will also be sharing some recipes with eggs and meat. Hopefully that provides some clarity.</p>

				// Used by Gallery Custom Links to handle tenacious Lightboxes
				jQuery(document).ready(function () {

					function mgclInit() {
						if (jQuery.fn.off) {
							jQuery('.no-lightbox, .no-lightbox img').off('click'); // jQuery 1.7+
						}
						else {
							jQuery('.no-lightbox, .no-lightbox img').unbind('click'); // < jQuery 1.7
						}
						jQuery('a.no-lightbox').click(mgclOnClick);

						if (jQuery.fn.off) {
							jQuery('a.set-target').off('click'); // jQuery 1.7+
						}
						else {
							jQuery('a.set-target').unbind('click'); // < jQuery 1.7
						}
						jQuery('a.set-target').click(mgclOnClick);
					}

					function mgclOnClick() {
						if (!this.target || this.target == '' || this.target == '_self')
							window.location = this.href;
						else
							window.open(this.href,this.target);
						return false;
					}

					// From WP Gallery Custom Links
					// Reduce the number of  conflicting lightboxes
					function mgclAddLoadEvent(func) {
						var oldOnload = window.onload;
						if (typeof window.onload != 'function') {
							window.onload = func;
						} else {
							window.onload = function() {
								oldOnload();
								func();
							}
						}
					}

					mgclAddLoadEvent(mgclInit);
					mgclInit();

				});
